(<bold>B</bold>) Profiles of topoisomers in lanes 34&#8211;39 shown in (A) as determined by using NIH Image.</p></caption><graphic xlink:href="gkn465f6"/></fig>
To investigate whether sas2Delta affects the structure of silent chromatin, we compared the supercoiling of HML DNA in wild-type and sas2Delta strains. In strain 34, the modified HML locus was bracketed by two copies of FRT (Flp1p recombination target), the recognition site for the site-specific recombinase Flp1p (Figure 6A, top). Induction by galactose of a PGAL-FLP1 fusion gene resident elsewhere in the genome would lead to the expression of Flp1p and recombination between the FRT sites resulting in the excision of HML as a closed minichromosome circle. After being deproteinized, the supercoiling of the circle can be examined by gel electrophoresis in the presence of the DNA intercalator chloroquine (Figure 6A, strain 34). Deletion of SIR3 reduced the negative supercoiling of HML DNA by a linking number change (DeltaLk) of 7 (Figure 6, compare the centers of topoisomer distributions in strains 38 and 34; note more negatively supercoiled circles migrate more slowly under the condition used). The sas2Delta induced a reduction in negative supercoiling of HML DNA of a DeltaLk of 1 (Figure 6, compare 35 and 34). This effect was specific to silent HML, as sas2Delta did not reduce the negative supercoiling of derepressed HML in a sir- background (Figure 6, compare 39 and 38). Therefore, the supercoiling of HML (hence the configuration of silent chromatin) in a sas2Delta strain is in an intermediate state between fully silenced and derepressed states (Figure 6, compare 35 to 34 and 38). This is consistent with our result that sas2Delta reduced transcriptional silencing to an intermediate level (Figure 5). Figure 6.sas2Delta reduces the negative supercoiling of silent HML DNA. (A) Top, diagram of the modified HML locus in strains 34-39. The HML-E and -I silencers and a pair of FRTs were shown. Each strain bears a PGAL-FLP1 gene in the genome. Bottom, the topology of HML DNA in strains 34-39. DNA isolated from each strain was subjected to agarose gel electrophoresis in the presence of 13 mug/ml chloroquine. Under this condition, more negatively supercoiled circles migrate more slowly. After Southern blotting, topoisomers of the HML circle were detected by an HML-specific probe. The center of distribution of topoisomers in each lane was marked by a dot. The nicked/relaxed form of the HML circle was indicated as N. (B) Profiles of topoisomers in lanes 34-39 shown in (A) as determined by using NIH Image.
###end p 52

###begin p 54
###xml 3 12 3 8 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sas2&#916;</italic>

###xml 54 57 46 49 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>

###xml 72 74 64 66 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B17">17</xref>
###xml 75 77 67 69 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B19">19</xref>
###xml 151 154 143 146 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 265 267 257 259 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 274 276 266 268 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B15">15</xref>
###xml 325 329 317 321 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SIR1</italic>
###xml 425 428 417 420 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 440 442 432 434 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B19">19</xref>
###xml 443 445 435 437 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B39">39</xref>
###xml 448 451 440 443 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 555 558 547 550 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 583 592 575 580 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir1&#916;</italic>
###xml 647 648 635 636 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 644 648 632 636 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SIR<sup>+</sup></italic>
###xml 661 664 649 652 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 695 696 683 684 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 692 696 680 684 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir<sup>&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 709 712 697 700 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 729 737 717 725 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 779 798 767 778 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sas2&#916; sir1&#916;</italic>
###xml 847 850 827 830 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 891 892 871 872 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 888 892 868 872 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir<sup>&#8722;</sup></italic>
###xml 900 908 880 888 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 941 950 921 926 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sas2&#916;</italic>
###xml 955 964 931 936 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir1&#916;</italic>
###xml 1008 1011 980 983 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 1059 1068 1031 1036 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sas2&#916;</italic>
###xml 1079 1082 1047 1050 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 1098 1107 1066 1071 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir1&#916;</italic>
###xml 1120 1122 1084 1086 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B13">13</xref>
###xml 1123 1125 1087 1089 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B17">17</xref>
###xml 1126 1128 1090 1092 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B19">19</xref>
As sas2Delta and sir1Delta have a synthetic effect on HML silencing (13,17,19), we tested whether they also have a synthetic effect on the topology of HML DNA. Sir1p is believed to be involved in the establishment but not the maintenance of silent chromatin at the HM loci (15). Single-cell assays revealed that a culture of SIR1 null cells consists of two populations of mitotically stable cells that differ in the state of HML silencing (19,39). HML is silenced in one population of cells, but derepressed in the other. Consistently, the topoisomers of HML circles isolated from a sir1Delta culture appear to be a mixture of topoisomers from SIR+ cells where HML is silenced and those from sir- cells where HML is derepressed (Figure 6, compare 36 to 34 and 38). However, in a sas2Delta sir1Delta double mutant, there was only one population of HML circles, which is similar to that in sir- cells (Figure 6, compare 37 and 38). Therefore, sas2Delta and sir1Delta have a synthetic effect on the topology of HML DNA, which is consistent with the finding that sas2Delta abolished HML silencing in a sir1Delta background (13,17,19).
###end p 54
###begin title 55
###xml 20 29 20 25 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sas2&#916;</italic>
###xml 34 40 30 36 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">orc5-1</italic>
Synthetic effect of sas2Delta and orc5-1 on transcriptional silencing
###end title 55
###begin p 56
###xml 57 66 57 62 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sas2&#916;</italic>
###xml 71 74 67 70 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">orc</italic>
###xml 221 227 217 223 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">orc5-1</italic>
###xml 231 240 227 232 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sas2&#916;</italic>
###xml 270 274 262 266 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">URA3</italic>
###xml 298 301 290 293 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 314 322 306 314 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F7">Figure 7</xref>
###xml 361 377 353 365 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sas2&#916; orc5-1</italic>
###xml 404 408 392 396 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">URA3</italic>
###xml 420 428 408 416 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F7">Figure 7</xref>
###xml 460 464 448 452 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SAS2</italic>
###xml 481 484 469 472 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 501 507 489 495 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">orc5-1</italic>
Given the aforementioned functional interactions between sas2Delta and orc mutants regarding cell growth and DNA replication, we asked whether they also interact to affect transcriptional silencing. We showed that either orc5-1 or sas2Delta alone reduced silencing of a URA3 reporter integrated at HMR in W303-1B (Figure 7, compare 41 and 42 to 40 on FOA), and sas2Delta orc5-1 double mutation abolished URA3 silencing (Figure 7, compare 43 to 40). Therefore, SAS2 is required for HMR silencing in an orc5-1 mutant.
###end p 56
###begin title 57
DISCUSSION
###end title 57
###begin title 58
###xml 19 23 19 23 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SAS2</italic>
A positive role of SAS2 in DNA replication
###end title 58
###begin p 59
###xml 169 170 169 170 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B4">4</xref>
###xml 502 503 502 503 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B9">9</xref>
###xml 588 592 588 592 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HAT1</italic>
###xml 645 648 645 648 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">orc</italic>
###xml 658 660 658 660 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B12">12</xref>
###xml 737 739 737 739 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B40">40</xref>
###xml 943 945 943 945 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B12">12</xref>
###xml 946 948 946 948 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B40">40</xref>
###xml 1097 1099 1097 1099 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B41">41</xref>
###xml 1100 1102 1100 1102 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B42">42</xref>
###xml 1368 1370 1368 1370 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B42">42</xref>
###xml 281 286 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 457 462 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 538 543 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
The initiation of DNA replication in eukaryotes depends on the assembly of the pre-RC via the sequential binding to the origin of ORC, Cdc6p, Cdt1p and the MCM complex (4). We have presented evidence suggesting that the HAT Sas2p plays a positive role in replication initiation in yeast. This is in line with the notion that chromatin structure regulates origin function. It has been shown that increasing histone acetylation around a replication origin in yeast enables it to fire earlier in S phase (9). Recently, it was found that the yeast HAT Hat1p physically interacts with ORC and HAT1 deletion exacerbates the temperature-sensitivity of orc mutants (12). Hat1p acetylates histone H4-K5, K12 and, to a lesser extent, histone H2A (40), and it may contribute to replication initiation by modifying nucleosomes near the origins. There is also evidence suggesting that Hat1p contributes to chromatin assembly during replication elongation (12,40). In vertebrates, Hbo1p, a member of the MYST family of HATs, has been shown to interact with ORC and MCM and positively regulate pre-RC formation (41,42). Depletion of Hbo1p does not affect chromatin binding of ORC and Cdc6p but prevents the recruitment of the MCM complex. It is proposed that Hbo1p facilitates MCM loading by acetylating chromatin at the origin and/or components of the pre-RC complex such as Orc2p (42).
###end p 59
###begin p 60
###xml 15 19 15 19 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SAS2</italic>
###xml 30 39 30 35 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sas2&#916;</italic>
###xml 169 175 165 171 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">orc2-1</italic>
###xml 186 194 182 190 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 569 573 565 569 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ARS1</italic>
###xml 633 642 629 634 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sas2&#916;</italic>
###xml 688 692 680 684 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ARS1</italic>
###xml 709 715 701 707 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">orc2-1</italic>
###xml 723 731 715 723 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F4">Figure 4</xref>
###xml 983 985 975 977 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B43">43</xref>
###xml 1236 1238 1228 1230 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B18">18</xref>
###xml 1239 1241 1231 1233 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B44">44</xref>
We showed that SAS2 deletion (sas2Delta) does not affect DNA replication in the presence of an intact ORC, but reduces origin firing when ORC function is compromised by orc2-1 mutation (Figure 3). Sas2p's role in DNA replication may overlap with that of other factors involved in ORC function such as Hat1p. It is not known whether Sas2p directly interacts with ORC like Hat1p and Hbo1p. Sas2p may help ORC function by acetylating histones near origins. We tested the possibility that Sas2p contributes to the formation of proper chromatin structure at origins such as ARS1 that is required for origin firing. However, we found that sas2Delta caused no significant change in chromatin at ARS1 in wild-type or orc2-1 cells (Figure 4). It is also possible that H4-K16 acetylation by Sas2p helps an origin fire by disrupting higher order chromatin structure. This is based on the finding that H4-K16 acetylation is inhibitory to 30 nm fiber structure formation from a nucleosome array (43). In addition, Sas2p may also contribute to chromatin assembly during DNA replication. Consistent with this notion is the finding that Sas2p physically interacts with CAF-I and Asf1p, two factors that mediate chromatin assembly during DNA synthesis (18,44).
###end p 60
###begin p 61
###xml 42 46 42 46 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ARS1</italic>
###xml 48 54 48 54 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ARS305</italic>
###xml 98 104 98 104 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">orc2-1</italic>
###xml 109 118 109 114 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sas2&#916;</italic>
###xml 141 147 137 143 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ARS305</italic>
###xml 180 188 176 184 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 191 197 187 193 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ARS305</italic>
###xml 215 219 211 215 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ARS1</italic>
###xml 259 263 255 259 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ARS1</italic>
###xml 302 308 298 304 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ARS305</italic>
###xml 354 362 350 358 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 385 391 381 387 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ARS305</italic>
###xml 467 475 463 471 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">Figure 3</xref>
###xml 551 557 547 553 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ARS305</italic>
###xml 622 626 618 622 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ARS1</italic>
We found, interestingly, that compared to ARS1, ARS305 firing was significantly less sensitive to orc2-1 and sas2Delta despite the fact that ARS305 is also an early-firing origin (Figure 3). ARS305 is distinct from ARS1 in sequence and structure. Whereas the ARS1 contains ACS, B1, B2 and B3 elements, ARS305 contains ACS, B1 and B4 but lacks B2 and B3 (Figure 3B; ref. 45). Moreover, ARS305 contains a DUE (DNA unwinding element) that is essential for its function (Figure 3B; ref. 46). The unique presence of this DUE sequence may be the reason why ARS305 firing is less dependent on the functions of ORC and Sas2p than ARS1.
###end p 61
###begin p 62
###xml 77 81 77 81 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SAS2</italic>
###xml 86 89 86 89 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ORC</italic>
###xml 149 158 149 154 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sas2&#916;</italic>
###xml 170 176 166 172 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">orc2-1</italic>
###xml 189 191 185 187 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B13">13</xref>
###xml 192 194 188 190 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B14">14</xref>
###xml 223 229 219 225 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">orc2-1</italic>
###xml 255 261 251 257 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">orc5-1</italic>
###xml 450 456 446 452 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">orc2-1</italic>
###xml 461 467 457 463 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">orc5-1</italic>
###xml 528 534 524 530 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 536 538 532 534 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B31">31</xref>
###xml 587 593 583 589 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">orc2-1</italic>
###xml 692 698 688 694 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">orc2-1</italic>
###xml 831 839 815 823 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 929 940 913 924 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">MATa orc2-1</italic>
###xml 1092 1098 1070 1076 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">orc2-1</italic>
###xml 1100 1108 1078 1086 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 1154 1160 1132 1138 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">orc5-1</italic>
###xml 1238 1247 1216 1221 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sas2&#916;</italic>
###xml 1289 1295 1263 1269 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">orc2-1</italic>
###xml 1300 1306 1274 1280 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">orc5-1</italic>
###xml 1352 1360 1326 1334 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 1478 1487 1452 1457 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sas2&#916;</italic>
###xml 1500 1506 1470 1476 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">orc2-1</italic>
###xml 1519 1521 1489 1491 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B13">13</xref>
###xml 1522 1524 1492 1494 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B14">14</xref>
###xml 1605 1614 1575 1580 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sas2&#916;</italic>
Our results demonstrating a synthetic genetic/functional interaction between SAS2 and ORC genes are apparently contrary to the previous finding that sas2Delta suppressed orc2-1 phenotypes (13,14). The temperature-sensitive orc2-1 and, to a lesser extent, orc5-1 mutants exhibit slow growth phenotypes even at permissive temperatures. It is possible that a spontaneous secondary mutation that suppresses the growth defect exists in one or more of the orc2-1 and orc5-1 mutants used in this and/or other studies. In fact, Shimada et al. (31) demonstrated that their batch of a widely used orc2-1 mutant JRY125 had an extragenic suppressor mutation that mitigated the temperature sensitivity of orc2-1 so that cells could grow at 30degreesC (but not higher temperatures). The JRY125 derivatives we made were not viable at 30degreesC (Figure 1B), and therefore did not seem to contain the additional mutation. On the other hand, our MATa orc2-1 strain was able to grow, albeit slowly, at 30degreesC, and therefore might possess a secondary mutation that partially suppresses the growth defect of orc2-1 (Figure 1). There has been no report regarding whether orc5-1 mutants contain extragenic suppressor mutations. Nevertheless, the fact that sas2Delta showed synthetic growth defect with both orc2-1 and orc5-1 in three genetic backgrounds in this report (Figure 1) strongly supports the notion that Sas2p plays a positive role in ORC-mediated functions. As for previous results of sas2Delta suppressing orc2-1 phenotypes (13,14), it is possible that an extragenic suppressor mutation alone, or together with sas2Delta, was responsible for the suppression.
###end p 62
###begin title 63
###xml 19 23 19 23 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SAS2</italic>
A positive role of SAS2 in transcriptional silencing
###end title 63
###begin p 64
###xml 32 36 32 36 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SAS2</italic>
###xml 136 140 136 140 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SAS2</italic>
###xml 216 218 216 218 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B13">13</xref>
###xml 219 224 219 224 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B17 B18 B19">17&#8211;19</xref>
###xml 539 542 539 542 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 550 553 550 553 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 580 589 580 585 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sas2&#916;</italic>
###xml 640 645 636 641 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR-E</italic>
###xml 647 652 643 648 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML-E</italic>
###xml 657 662 653 658 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML-I</italic>
###xml 732 737 728 733 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML-E</italic>
###xml 739 747 735 743 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F5">Figure 5</xref>
###xml 766 771 762 767 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR-E</italic>
###xml 838 847 834 839 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sas2&#916;</italic>
###xml 849 864 841 856 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F5 F7">Figures 5 and 7</xref>
###xml 895 899 887 891 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">URA3</italic>
###xml 1012 1016 1004 1008 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SAS2</italic>
###xml 1167 1171 1159 1163 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SAS2</italic>
###xml 1350 1352 1342 1344 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B20">20</xref>
###xml 1353 1355 1345 1347 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B21">21</xref>
###xml 1407 1409 1399 1401 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 1441 1450 1433 1438 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sas2&#916;</italic>
###xml 1500 1503 1488 1491 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 1508 1511 1496 1499 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 1583 1585 1571 1573 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
Previous studies on the role of SAS2 in transcriptional silencing yielded conflicting results, with some suggesting a positive role for SAS2 in silencing, while others concluding that Sas2p was a negative regulator (13,17-19). However, the silencing assays used in these studies were distinct from each other concerning the silencing reporter, the silent locus, and/or the genetic background, making it difficult to compare the results directly. In this work, we examined whether the intrinsic properties and/or the context of a silencer (HML versus HMR) affected its response to sas2Delta. We showed that the function of each of silencers HMR-E, HML-E and HML-I was reduced to an intermediate level when put in the same context of HML-E (Figure 5). The activity of HMR-E in its native context is also reduced to an intermediate level by sas2Delta (Figures 5 and 7). The same silencing reporter URA3 was used in all our experiments so the results can be readily compared directly. These results demonstrate that SAS2 plays a positive role in the function of any of the tested silencers regardless of their genomic contexts, which are consistent with the finding that SAS2 is required for telomeric silencing. Acetylation of histone H4-K16 by Sas2p in euchromatin was proposed to prevent ectopic spreading Sir complex from telomeric silent chromatin (20,21). This model may also apply to silent chromatin at HM loci. According to this model, sas2Delta allows a portion of Sir proteins to leave silent HML and HMR and spread into euchromatin regions, thereby reducing Sir abundance at HM loci. As a result, silent chromatin adopts an intermediate state between fully silent and fully derepressed structures.
###end p 64
###begin p 65
###xml 46 50 46 50 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SAS2</italic>
###xml 55 58 55 58 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ORC</italic>
###xml 217 226 217 222 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sas2&#916;</italic>
###xml 231 237 227 233 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">orc5-1</italic>
###xml 265 268 261 264 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR</italic>
###xml 280 288 276 284 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F7">Figure 7</xref>
###xml 427 429 423 425 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B15">15</xref>
###xml 562 564 558 560 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B47">47</xref>
Given the functional interactions between the SAS2 and ORC genes in DNA replication, we envision that Sas2p may also regulate silencing by affecting ORC function at the silencer. This is supported by our finding that sas2Delta and orc5-1 have a synthetic effect on HMR silencing (Figure 7). ORC bound to a silencer contributes to the establishment of silent chromatin by recruiting Sir1p, which interacts with the Sir complex (15). In addition, ORC also directs nucleosome positioning at the silencer that affects the efficiency and directionality of silencing (47). It is possible that Sas2p-mediated histone acetylation near the silencer facilitates one or both of these ORC-mediated processes.
###end p 65
###begin p 66
###xml 71 75 71 75 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SAS2</italic>
###xml 119 130 119 130 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F5 F6 F7">Figures 5&#8211;7</xref>
###xml 185 189 185 189 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SAS2</italic>
###xml 235 240 235 240 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR-E</italic>
###xml 289 291 289 291 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B13">13</xref>
###xml 292 294 292 294 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B17">17</xref>
###xml 339 344 339 344 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HMR-E</italic>
###xml 366 370 366 370 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SAS2</italic>
It is noteworthy that our experiments demonstrating a positive role of SAS2 in silencing involved wild-type silencers (Figures 5-7), while previous studies reporting a negative role of SAS2 in silencing employed a mutated or synthetic HMR-E silencer that is weaker than the wild-type one (13,17). It is not clear why wild-type and mutated HMR-E silencers respond to SAS2 in opposite ways.
###end p 66
###begin title 67
Role of Sas2p in maintaining a fully silenced state of chromatin
###end title 67
###begin p 68
###xml 14 23 14 19 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sas2&#916;</italic>
###xml 61 64 57 60 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 79 81 71 73 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Lk</italic>
###xml 88 96 80 88 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 131 138 123 126 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#916;Lk</italic>
###xml 154 163 142 147 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir3&#916;</italic>
###xml 165 173 149 157 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">Figure 6</xref>
###xml 216 225 200 205 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sas2&#916;</italic>
###xml 301 303 281 283 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HM</italic>
###xml 310 325 290 305 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F5 F7">Figures 5 and 7</xref>
###xml 346 349 326 329 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 446 449 426 429 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">SIR</italic>
###xml 449 450 429 430 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">+</sup>
###xml 493 494 473 474 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 490 494 470 474 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sir<sup>&#8722;</sup></italic>
We found that sas2Delta reduced the negative supercoiling of HML DNA by a DeltaLk of 1 (Figure 6). This reduction is less than the DeltaLk of 7 caused by sir3Delta (Figure 6), but is consistent with the finding that sas2Delta decreases but does not completely abolish transcriptional silencing at the HM loci (Figures 5 and 7), and suggests that HML chromatin assumes an intermediate state that is distinct from both the fully silenced state (in SIR+ cells) and fully derepressed state (in sir- cells).
###end p 68
###begin p 69
###xml 277 279 273 275 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Lk</italic>
###xml 314 322 310 318 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
###xml 324 326 320 322 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B48">48</xref>
###xml 525 527 521 523 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B49">49</xref>
###xml 599 602 595 598 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HML</italic>
###xml 739 741 735 737 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B50">50</xref>
###xml 742 744 738 740 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B51">51</xref>
###xml 797 806 793 798 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">sas2&#916;</italic>
The topology of eukaryotic DNA is determined by multiple factors including the density of nucleosomes along the DNA and the conformation of individual nucleosomes. The major contribution to the negative supercoiling of DNA is its wrapping into nucleosomes with an average DeltaLk of about -1 per nucleosome formed in vitro (48). Changing the conformation of a nucleosome may alter the number of supercoils constrained on it. For example, acetylation of the core histones reduces the negative supercoiling of nucleosomal DNA (49). The higher negative supercoiling of DNA in silent versus derepressed HML locus is a reflection of increased regularity and stability of nucleosomes as wells as reduced histone acetylation in silent chromatin (50,51). The reduction of negative supercoiling induced by sas2Delta might be the result of a decrease in nucleosome density/stability and/or conformational changes of nucleosomes, but our preliminary chromatin mapping results suggest that the former is unlikely the case (Zou,Y. and Bi,X. unpublished results).
###end p 69
